<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1218072481"><table class="infobox"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" </td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG/220px-Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG/330px-Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG/440px-Xiaomi_Redmi_Note.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a><figcaption>Xiaomi's Redmi Note</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Xiaomi_Store.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Xiaomi_Store.jpg/220px-Xiaomi_Store.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Xiaomi_Store.jpg/330px-Xiaomi_Store.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Xiaomi_Store.jpg/440px-Xiaomi_Store.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="640" /></a><figcaption>A Xiaomi Exclusive Service Centre for customer support in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a></figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Xiaomi Corporation</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʃ/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">ʃ</span><span title="/aʊ/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">aʊ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B0%8F%E7%B1%B3" class="extiw" title="wikt:小米">小米</a></span>), commonly known as <b>Xiaomi</b> and registered as <b>Xiaomi Inc.</b>, is a Chinese designer and manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a> and related <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_appliance" title="Home appliance">home appliances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Auto" title="Xiaomi Auto">automobiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Household_hardware" title="Household hardware">household hardware</a>. It is the second-largest manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CNET_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNET-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> most of which run on the <a href="/wiki/MIUI" title="MIUI">MIUI</a> (now <a href="/wiki/HyperOS" class="mw-redirect" title="HyperOS">HyperOS</a>) <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>, which is based on the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> operating system. The company is ranked 338th and is the youngest company on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500"><i>Fortune</i> Global 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader">Xiaomi stores</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">In <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>, China</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Xiaomi_Store_Portugal.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Xiaomi_Store_Portugal.jpg/200px-Xiaomi_Store_Portugal.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" class="thumbcaption">In <a href="/wiki/Loul%C3%A9" title="Loulé">Loulé</a>, Portugal</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:XiaomiHangzhouStore.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" class="thumbcaption">In <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, China</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Xiaomi was founded in 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> by <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a> along with six associates. Lei had founded <a href="/wiki/Kingsoft" title="Kingsoft">Kingsoft</a> as well as Joyo.com, the latter of which he sold to <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> for $75&#160;million in 2004. In August 2011, Xiaomi released its first smartphone and, by 2014, it had the largest market share of smartphones sold in China. Initially the company only sold its products online; however, it later opened <a href="/wiki/Brick_and_mortar" title="Brick and mortar">brick and mortar</a> stores.<sup id="cite_ref-CW-Kan-so_cheap_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CW-Kan-so_cheap-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> By 2015, it was developing a wide range of consumer electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, the company sold 149.4&#160;million smartphones and its MIUI (now HyperOS) mobile operating system has over 500 million monthly active users.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As of 2023, Xiaomi is the third-largest seller of smartphones worldwide, with a market share of about 12%, according to Counterpoint.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Its presence led some people to call Xiaomi the "Apple of China".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It has come up with its own range of wearable items.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It also is a major manufacturer of appliances including <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">televisions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flashlight" title="Flashlight">flashlights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">unmanned aerial vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Air_purifier" title="Air purifier">air purifiers</a> using its <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">Internet of things</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Smart_Home" title="Xiaomi Smart Home">Xiaomi Smart Home</a> product ecosystems.
</p><p>Xiaomi keeps its prices close to its <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_cost" title="Manufacturing cost">manufacturing costs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_materials" title="Bill of materials">bill of materials</a> costs by keeping most of its products in the market for 18 months, longer than most smartphone companies.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The company also uses <a href="/wiki/Inventory_optimization" title="Inventory optimization">inventory optimization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deal-of-the-day" title="Deal-of-the-day">flash sales</a> to keep its inventory low.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CW-Kan-so_cheap_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CW-Kan-so_cheap-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Xiaomi_products" title="List of Xiaomi products">List of Xiaomi products</a></div>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932013"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2013">2010–2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2010–2013"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 6 April 2010 Xiaomi was co-founded by <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a> and six others:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lin_Bin" title="Lin Bin">Lin Bin</a> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">林斌</span></span>), vice president of the <a href="/wiki/Google_China" title="Google China">Google China</a> Institute of Engineering</li>
<li>Zhou Guangping (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">周光平</span></span>), senior director of the <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola</a> Beijing R&amp;D center</li>
<li>Liu De (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">刘德</span></span>), department chair of the Department of Industrial Design at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Science_and_Technology_Beijing" title="University of Science and Technology Beijing">University of Science and Technology Beijing</a></li>
<li>Li Wanqiang (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">黎万强</span></span>), general manager of <a href="/wiki/Kingsoft" title="Kingsoft">Kingsoft</a> Dictionary</li>
<li>Huang Jiangji (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">黄江吉</span></span>), principal development manager</li>
<li>Hong Feng (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">洪峰</span></span>), senior product manager for Google China</li></ul>
<p>Lei had founded <a href="/wiki/Kingsoft" title="Kingsoft">Kingsoft</a> as well as Joyo.com, the latter of which he sold to <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> for $75&#160;million in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Imitation_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imitation-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> At the time of the founding of the company, Lei was dissatisfied with the products of other mobile phone manufacturers and thought he could make a better product.
</p><p>On 16 August 2010, Xiaomi launched its first <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>-based firmware <a href="/wiki/MIUI" title="MIUI">MIUI</a> (Now <a href="/wiki/HyperOS" class="mw-redirect" title="HyperOS">HyperOS</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the company raised $41&#160;million in a <a href="/wiki/Series_A_round" title="Series A round">Series A round</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-raises_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raises-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2011, the company launched its first phone, the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Mi_1" title="Xiaomi Mi 1">Xiaomi Mi 1</a>. The device had Xiaomi's MIUI firmware along with Android installation.<sup id="cite_ref-Imitation_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imitation-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2011, the company raised $90&#160;million in a Series B round.<sup id="cite_ref-raises_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raises-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2012, the company raised $216&#160;million of funding in a Series C round at a $4&#160;billion valuation. Institutional investors participating in the first round of funding included <a href="/wiki/Temasek_Holdings" title="Temasek Holdings">Temasek Holdings</a>, <a href="/wiki/IDG_Capital" title="IDG Capital">IDG Capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qiming_Venture_Partners" title="Qiming Venture Partners">Qiming Venture Partners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Imitation_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imitation-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2013, the company hired <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Barra" title="Hugo Barra">Hugo Barra</a> from <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, where he served as vice president of product management for the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> platform.<sup id="cite_ref-poached_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poached-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He was employed as vice president of Xiaomi to expand the company outside of mainland China, making Xiaomi the first company selling smartphones to <a href="/wiki/Executive_search" title="Executive search">poach</a> a senior staffer from Google's Android team. He left the company in February 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2013, Xiaomi announced its <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Mi_3" title="Xiaomi Mi 3">Xiaomi Mi 3</a> smartphone and an Android-based 47-inch 3D-capable Smart TV assembled by <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> TV manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Wistron" title="Wistron">Wistron</a> of Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2013, it became the fifth-most-used smartphone brand in China.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Xiaomi sold 18.7&#160;million smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2017">2014–2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2014–2017"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2014, Xiaomi announced its expansion outside China, with an international headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2014, Xiaomi purchased the <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a> mi.com for a record <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3.6 million</span>, the most expensive domain name ever bought in China, replacing xiaomi.com as the company's main domain name.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, Xiaomi acquired a 24.7% stake in Roborock.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, Xiaomi raised US$1.1&#160;billion at a valuation of over US$45&#160;billion, making it one of the most valuable private technology companies in the world. The financing round was led by Hong Kong-based technology fund All-Stars Investment Limited, a fund run by former <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a> analyst Richard Ji.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the company sold over 60 million smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, 94% of the company's revenue came from mobile phone sales.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, <a href="/wiki/Ratan_Tata" title="Ratan Tata">Ratan Tata</a> acquired a stake in Xiaomi.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 June 2015, Xiaomi announced its expansion into Brazil with the launch of locally manufactured <a href="/wiki/Redmi" title="Redmi">Redmi</a> 2; it was the first time the company assembled a smartphone outside of China.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> 
However, the company left Brazil in the second half of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 February 2016, Xiaomi launched the Mi5, powered by the <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Qualcomm_Snapdragon_systems_on_chips" title="List of Qualcomm Snapdragon systems on chips">Snapdragon 820</a> processor.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 March 2016, Xiaomi launched the <a href="/wiki/Redmi_Note_3" title="Redmi Note 3">Redmi Note 3</a> Pro in India, the first smartphone to be powered by a Qualcomm Snapdragon 650 processor.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 May 2016, Xiaomi launched the Mi Max, powered by the Qualcomm Snapdragon 650/652 processor.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, the company acquired patents from <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2016, Xiaomi launched sales in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) through a partnership with ABC Data.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in September 2016, the Xiaomi Mi Robot vacuum was released by Roborock.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 October 2016, Xiaomi launched the Mi Mix, powered by the Qualcomm Snapdragon 821 processor.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 March 2017, Xiaomi announced that it planned to set up a second manufacturing unit in India in partnership with contract manufacturer Foxconn.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 April 2017, Xiaomi launched the Mi6, powered by the Qualcomm Snapdragon 835 processor.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, the company entered into a patent licensing agreement with <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 September 2017, Xiaomi released <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Mi_A1" title="Xiaomi Mi A1">Xiaomi Mi A1</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Android_One" title="Android One">Android One</a> smartphone under the slogan: Created by Xiaomi, Powered by Google. Xiaomi stated started working with Google for the Mi A1 Android One smartphone earlier in 2017. An alternate version of the phone was also available with MIUI, the MI 5X.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Xiaomi opened Mi Stores in India, Pakistan and Bangladesh. The EU's first Mi Store was opened in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, Greece in October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In Q3 2017, Xiaomi overtook Samsung to become the largest smartphone brand in India. Xiaomi sold 9.2&#160;million units during the quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 7 November 2017, Xiaomi commenced sales in Spain and western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.932021"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2021">2018–2021</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2018–2021"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2018, Xiaomi announced a smartphone gaming brand called Black Shark. It had 6GB of RAM coupled with Snapdragon 845 SoC, and was priced at $508, which was cheaper than its competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 May 2018, Xiaomi announced the launch of Mi Music and Mi Video to offer "value-added internet services" in India.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 3 May 2018, Xiaomi announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/3_(telecommunications)" class="mw-redirect" title="3 (telecommunications)">3</a> to sell smartphones in the United Kingdom, Ireland, Austria, Denmark, and Sweden<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2018, Xiaomi began selling smart home products in the United States through <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, Xiaomi became a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> via an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Stock_Exchange" title="Hong Kong Stock Exchange">Hong Kong Stock Exchange</a>, raising $4.72&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 August 2018, Xiaomi announced that Holitech Technology Co. Ltd., Xiaomi's top supplier, would invest up to $200&#160;million over the next three years to set up a major new plant in India.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2018, the company announced <a href="/wiki/POCO_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="POCO (company)">POCO</a> as a mid-range <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> line, first launching in India.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Q4 of 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Pocophone_F1" title="Xiaomi Pocophone F1">Xiaomi Pocophone F1</a> became the best-selling smartphone sold online in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The Pocophone was sometimes referred to as the "flagship killer" for offering high-end specifications at an affordable price.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2019, the company announced that it would launch more than 10 <a href="/wiki/5G_network_slicing" title="5G network slicing">5G</a> phones in 2020, including the Mi 10/10 Pro with 5G functionality.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 November 2019, Xiaomi announced that it would enter the Japanese market.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> It established a subsidiary, Xiaomi Japan, as parts of its effort to enter the Japanese smartphone market.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 January 2020, POCO India became a separate sub-brand of Xiaomi with entry-level and mid-range devices,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> followed by its global counterpart on 24 November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, Xiaomi launched their first foldable phone, the Mi Mix Fold. Powered by Qualcomm Snapdragon 888 with an 8.01-inch foldable AMOLED display when open and a 6.5-inch external display when folded.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In March 2020, Xiaomi showcased its new 40W wireless charging solution, which was able to fully charge a smartphone with a 4,000mAh battery from flat in 40 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2020, Xiaomi became the third-largest smartphone maker in the world by shipment volume, shipping 46.2&#160;million handsets in Q3 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 March 2021, Xiaomi announced its intention to invest US$10&#160;billion in <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> over the following ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On 31 March 2021, Xiaomi announced a new logo for the company, designed by <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Hara" title="Kenya Hara">Kenya Hara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2021, Xiaomi became the second largest smartphone maker in the world, according to Canalys.<sup id="cite_ref-canalys-21-q2_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canalys-21-q2-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It also surpassed <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> for the first time in Europe, making it the second-largest in Europe according to Counterpoint.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In August 2021, the company acquired autonomous driving company Deepmotion for $77&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2021, Xiaomi announced the Xiaomi 12 and Xiaomi 12 Pro. The phones are powered by the Snapdragon 8 Gen 1 chipset.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_2022">Since 2022</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Since 2022"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2022, Xiaomi officially joined the Car Connectivity Consortium (CCC) board.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2022, the Indian court lifted the $725&#160;million freeze on Xiaomi by federal agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, Xiaomi established Zhuhai Xinshi Semiconductor Technology Co., Ltd., with a registered capital of 200 million RMB. The business scope includes: integrated circuit manufacturing, integrated circuit chip design and services, integrated circuit chip and product manufacturing, integrated circuit design, manufacturing of specialized equipment for semiconductor devices, manufacturing of semiconductor discrete devices, manufacturing of semiconductor lighting devices etc. The company is jointly held by Xiaomi's affiliated company Hubei Xiaomi Changjiang Industrial Fund Management and others.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2022, Xiaomi and its sub-brand POCO combined held a 42% market share in the Russian smartphone market, ranking first.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 August 2022, Xiaomi India elevated COO Murali Krishnan B as president, responsible for the company's daily operations, services, public affairs, and strategic projects, stating that he would continue to work towards strengthening the company's commitment to the Made in India and Digital India initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 August 2022, the 2022 Fortune Global 500 list was released, with Xiaomi Group ranking 266th, a rise of 72 positions compared to the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2022, Xiaomi announced that the global cumulative sales of the Redmi Note series had exceeded 300 million units.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 February 2023, Redmi released a 300W fast charging technology, claiming that it can charge a 4100mAh battery by 10% in just 3 seconds, 50% in 2 minutes and 13 seconds, and fully charge it within 5 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Innovation_and_development">Innovation and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Innovation and development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the 2021 review of <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">WIPO</a>'s annual <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Indicators" title="World Intellectual Property Indicators">World Intellectual Property Indicators</a> Xiaomi was ranked as 2nd in the world, with 216 designs in industrial design registrations being published under the <a href="/wiki/Hague_Agreement_Concerning_the_International_Deposit_of_Industrial_Designs" title="Hague Agreement Concerning the International Deposit of Industrial Designs">Hague System</a> during 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> This position is up on their previous 3rd-place ranking in 2019 for 111 industrial design registrations being published.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 February 2022, Lei released a statement on Weibo to announce plans for Xiaomi to enter the high-end smartphone market and surpass Apple as the top seller of premium smartphones in China in three years. To achieve that goal, Xiaomi will invest US$15.7&#160;billion in R&amp;D over the next five years, and the company will benchmark its products and user experience against Apple's product lines.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Lei described the new strategy as a "life-or-death battle for our development" in his Weibo post, after Xiaomi's market share in China contracted over consecutive quarters, from 17% to 14% between Q2 and Q3 2021, dipping further to 13.2% as of Q4 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a recent report by Canalys, Xiaomi leads Indian smartphone sales in Q1. Xiaomi is one of the leaders of the smartphone makers in India which maintains device affordability.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, Xiaomi announced and debuted the company's humanoid robot prototype to the public, while the current state of the robot is very limited in its abilities, the announcement was made to mark the companies ambitions to integrate AI into its product designs as well as develop their humanoid robot project into the future.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_vehicles">Electric vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Electric vehicles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2021, Xiaomi announced a 10 billion USD investment into electric vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In late 2023 Xiaomi unveiled its first production vehicle, the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_SU7" title="Xiaomi SU7">Xiaomi SU7</a>, and publicly announced a goal to become one of the five largest automakers in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> On 28 March 2024, Xiaomi officially launched the SU7 sedan in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Partnerships"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg/220px-The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg/330px-The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg/440px-The_back_of_Xiaomi_12SU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3472" data-file-height="4640" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_12" title="Xiaomi 12">Xiaomi 12S Ultra</a> featured a "<a href="/wiki/Leica_Camera" title="Leica Camera">Leica</a> Summicron 1:1.9-4.1 / 13-120 ASPH camera system".</figcaption></figure>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Xiaomi_and_Harman_Kardon">Xiaomi and Harman Kardon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Xiaomi and Harman Kardon"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2021, <a href="/wiki/Harman_Kardon" title="Harman Kardon">Harman Kardon</a> collaborated with Xiaomi for its newest <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Mi_11" title="Xiaomi Mi 11">Xiaomi Mi 11</a> series are the first smartphones to feature with Harman Kardon-tuned dual speaker setup.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Xiaomi_and_Leica">Xiaomi and Leica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Xiaomi and Leica"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2022, <a href="/wiki/Leica_Camera" title="Leica Camera">Leica Camera</a> entered a strategic partnership with Xiaomi to jointly develop Leica cameras to be used in Xiaomi flagship <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a>, succeeding the partnership between <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a> and Leica. The first flagship smartphones under this new partnership were the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_12" title="Xiaomi 12">Xiaomi 12S Ultra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_MIX_Fold_2" title="Xiaomi MIX Fold 2">Xiaomi MIX Fold 2</a>, launched in July and August 2022, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Xiaomi_Studios">Xiaomi Studios</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Xiaomi Studios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2021, Xiaomi began collaborating with directors to create short films shot entirely using the <a href="/wiki/Xiaomi_Mi_11" title="Xiaomi Mi 11">Xiaomi Mi 11</a> line of phones. In 2022, they made two shorts with <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Henwick" title="Jessica Henwick">Jessica Henwick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The first, <i>Bus Girl</i> won several awards<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and was long-listed for Best British Short at the 2023 <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Corporate identity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_etymology">Name etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Name etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Xiaomi</i> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">小米</span></span>) is the Chinese word for "<a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In 2011 its CEO <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a> suggested there are more meanings than just the "millet and rice".<sup id="cite_ref-LeiJunName雷军名称_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeiJunName雷军名称-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> He linked the "Xiao" (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">小</span></span>) part to the <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> concept that "a single grain of rice of a Buddhist is as great as a mountain",<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> suggesting that Xiaomi wants to work from the little things, instead of starting by striving for perfection,<sup id="cite_ref-LeiJunName雷军名称_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeiJunName雷军名称-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> while "mi" (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">米</span></span>) is an acronym for Mobile Internet and also "mission impossible", referring to the obstacles encountered in starting the company.<sup id="cite_ref-LeiJunName雷军名称_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeiJunName雷军名称-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He also stated that he thinks the name is cute.<sup id="cite_ref-LeiJunName雷军名称_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeiJunName雷军名称-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 Lei Jun said that the name is about revolution and being able to bring innovation into a new area.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi's new "Rifle" processor<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> has given weight to several sources linking the latter meaning to the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Millet_plus_rifles" title="Millet plus rifles">"millet and rifle" (小米加步枪) revolutionary idiom</a><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo_and_mascot">Logo and mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Logo and mascot"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:104px;max-width:104px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Xiaomi_logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xiaomi_logo.svg/100px-Xiaomi_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="100" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xiaomi_logo.svg/150px-Xiaomi_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xiaomi_logo.svg/200px-Xiaomi_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">First Xiaomi logo<br /><span style="font-size:85%;">(2010–2021)</span></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Xiaomi_logo_(2021-).svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg/100px-Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="100" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg/150px-Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg/200px-Xiaomi_logo_%282021-%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Current logo<br /><span style="font-size:85%;">(2021–present)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg/220px-MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg/330px-MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg/440px-MiHomeTempleMallHongKong.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3052" /></a><figcaption>A Mi-Home store with the new logo</figcaption></figure>
<p>Xiaomi's first logo consisted of a single orange square with the letters "MI" in white located in the center of the square. This logo was in use until 31 March 2021, when a new logo, designed by well-known Japanese designer <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Hara" title="Kenya Hara">Kenya Hara</a>, replaced the old one, consisting of the same basic structure as the previous logo, but the square was replaced with a "<a href="/wiki/Squircle" title="Squircle">squircle</a>" with rounded corners instead, with the letters "MI" remaining identical to the previous logo, along with a slightly darker hue.
</p><p>Xiaomi's mascot, Mitu, is a white <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a> wearing an <a href="/wiki/Ushanka" title="Ushanka">Ushanka</a> (known locally as a "<a href="/wiki/Lei_Feng" title="Lei Feng">Lei Feng</a> hat" in China) with a red star and a red scarf around its neck.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Later on, the red star on the hat was replaced by the company's logo.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imitation_of_Apple_Inc.">Imitation of Apple Inc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Imitation of Apple Inc."><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Xiaomi has been accused of imitating <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-Amadeo_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amadeo-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hunger_marketing" title="Hunger marketing">hunger marketing</a> strategy of Xiaomi was described as riding on the back of the "cult of Apple".<sup id="cite_ref-Imitation_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imitation-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After reading a book about <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> in college, Xiaomi's chairman and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a>, carefully cultivated a <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> image, including jeans, dark shirts, and Jobs' announcement style at Xiaomi's earlier product announcements.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heard_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> He was characterized as a "counterfeit Jobs."<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, critics debated how many of Xiaomi's products were innovative,<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-poached_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poached-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PCWorld1_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCWorld1-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and how much of their innovation was just really good public relations.<sup id="cite_ref-PCWorld1_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCWorld1-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Others point out that while there are similarities to Apple, the ability to customize the software based upon user preferences through the use of Google's Android operating system sets Xiaomi apart.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi has also developed a much wider range of consumer products than Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violation_of_GNU_General_Public_License">Violation of GNU General Public License</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Violation of GNU General Public License"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2018, Xiaomi was criticized for its non-compliance with the terms of the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a>. The Android project's <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> kernel is licensed under the <a href="/wiki/Copyleft" title="Copyleft">copyleft</a> terms of the GPL, which requires Xiaomi to distribute the complete source code of the Android kernel and device trees for every Android device it distributes. By refusing to do so, or by unreasonably delaying these releases, Xiaomi is operating in violation of intellectual property law in China, as a <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">WIPO</a> state.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Prominent Android developer Francisco Franco publicly criticized Xiaomi's behaviour after repeated delays in the release of kernel source code.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi in 2013 said that it would release the kernel code.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The kernel source code was available on the <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a> website in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy_concerns_and_data_collection">Privacy concerns and data collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Privacy concerns and data collection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a company based in China, Xiaomi is obligated to share data with the Chinese government under the <a href="/wiki/Cybersecurity_Law_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Cybersecurity Law of the People&#39;s Republic of China">China Internet Security Law</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Intelligence_Law_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="National Intelligence Law of the People&#39;s Republic of China">National Intelligence Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> There were reports that Xiaomi's Cloud messaging service sends some private data, including call logs and contact information, to Xiaomi servers.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi later released an MIUI update that made cloud messaging optional and that no private data was sent to Xiaomi servers if the cloud messaging service was turned off.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 October 2014, Xiaomi announced that it was setting up servers outside of China for international users, citing improved services and compliance to regulations in several countries.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 October 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> issued a warning against Xiaomi phones, stating that they were a national threat as they sent user data to an agency of the Chinese government.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2019, researchers at <a href="/wiki/Check_Point" title="Check Point">Check Point</a> found a security breach in Xiaomi phone apps.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The security flaw was reported to be preinstalled.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 April 2020, <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> reported that Xiaomi extensively tracks use of its browsers, including private browser activity, phone metadata and device navigation, and more alarmingly, without secure encryption or <a href="/wiki/Data_anonymization" title="Data anonymization">data anonymization</a>, more invasively and to a greater extent than mainstream browsers. Xiaomi disputed the claims, while confirming that it did extensively collect browsing data, and saying that the data was not linked to any individuals and that users had consented to being tracked.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi posted a response stating that the collection of aggregated usage statistics data is used for internal analysis, and would not link any personally identifiable information to any of this data.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> However, after a follow-up by Gabriel Cirlig, the writer of the report, Xiaomi added an option to completely stop the information leak when using its browser in incognito mode.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Censorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 2021, amidst a political spat between <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(Lithuania)" title="Ministry of National Defence (Lithuania)">Ministry of National Defence</a> urged people to dispose the Chinese-made mobile phones and avoid buying new ones,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> after the <a href="/wiki/National_Cyber_Security_Centre_of_Lithuania" title="National Cyber Security Centre of Lithuania">National Cyber Security Centre of Lithuania</a> claimed that Xiaomi devices have built-in censorship capabilities that can be turned on remotely.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Xiaomi denied the accusations, saying that it "does not censor communications to or from its users", and that they would be engaging a third-party to assess the allegations. They also stated that regarding data privacy, it was compliant with two frameworks for following Europe's General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR), namely its ISO/IEC 27001 Information Security Management Standards and the ISO/IEC 27701 Privacy Information Management System.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_actions">Legal actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Legal actions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="State_administration_of_radio.2C_film_and_television_issue"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="State_administration_of_radio,_film_and_television_issue">State administration of radio, film and television issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: State administration of radio, film and television issue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2012, Xiaomi's smart set-top box stopped working one week after the launch due to the company having run foul of China's <a href="/wiki/National_Radio_and_Television_Administration" title="National Radio and Television Administration">National Radio and Television Administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The regulatory issues were overcome in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Misleading_sales_figures">Misleading sales figures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Misleading sales figures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fair_Trade_Commission_(Taiwan)" title="Fair Trade Commission (Taiwan)">Taiwanese Fair Trade Commission</a> investigated the flash sales and found that Xiaomi had sold fewer smartphones than advertised.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi claimed that the number of smartphones sold was 10,000 units each for the first two <a href="/wiki/Deal-of-the-day" title="Deal-of-the-day">flash sales</a>, and 8,000 units for the third one. However, FTC investigated the claims and found that Xiaomi sold 9,339 devices in the first flash sale, 9,492 units in the second one, and 7,389 for the third.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> It was found that during the first flash sale, Xiaomi had given 1,750 priority ‘F-codes’ to people who could place their orders without having to go through the flash sale, thus diminishing the stock that was publicly available. The FTC fined Xiaomi <a href="/wiki/New_Taiwan_dollar" title="New Taiwan dollar">NT$</a>600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shut_down_of_Australia_store">Shut down of Australia store</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Shut down of Australia store"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2014, Xiaomi Store Australia (an unrelated business) began selling Xiaomi mobile phones online in Australia through its website, XiaomiStore.com.au.<sup id="cite_ref-Oz_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oz-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> However, Xiaomi soon requested that the store be shut down by 25 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Oz_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oz-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> On 7 August 2014, shortly after sales were halted, the website was taken down.<sup id="cite_ref-Oz_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oz-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> An industry commentator described the action by Xiaomi to get the Australian website closed down as unprecedented, saying, "I’ve never come across this [before]. It would have to be a strategic move."<sup id="cite_ref-Oz_171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oz-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> At the time this left only one online vendor selling Xiaomi mobile phones into Australia, namely Yatango (formerly MobiCity), which was based in Hong Kong.<sup id="cite_ref-Oz_171-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oz-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> This business closed in late 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Temporary_ban_in_India_due_to_patent_infringement">Temporary ban in India due to patent infringement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Temporary ban in India due to patent infringement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 9 December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_High_Court" title="Delhi High Court">Delhi High Court</a> granted an <a href="/wiki/Ex_parte" title="Ex parte">ex parte</a> injunction that banned the import and sale of Xiaomi products in India. The injunction was issued in response to a complaint filed by Ericsson in connection with the infringement of its patent licensed under <a href="/wiki/Reasonable_and_non-discriminatory_licensing" title="Reasonable and non-discriminatory licensing">reasonable and non-discriminatory licensing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The injunction was applicable until 5 February 2015, the date on which the High Court was scheduled to summon both parties for a formal hearing of the case. On 16 December, the High Court granted permission to Xiaomi to sell its devices running on a Qualcomm-based processor until 8 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi then held various sales on <a href="/wiki/Flipkart" title="Flipkart">Flipkart</a>, including one on 30 December 2014. Its flagship Xiaomi Redmi Note 4G phone sold out in six seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> A judge extended the division bench's interim order, allowing Xiaomi to continue the sale of Qualcomm chipset-based handsets until March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="US_sanctions_due_to_ties_with_People.27s_Liberation_Army"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="US_sanctions_due_to_ties_with_People's_Liberation_Army">US sanctions due to ties with People's Liberation Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: US sanctions due to ties with People&#039;s Liberation Army"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2021, towards the end of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">presidency of Donald Trump</a>, the United States government named Xiaomi as a company "owned or controlled" by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People&#39;s Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> and thereby <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_13959" title="Executive Order 13959">prohibited</a> any American company or individual from investing in it.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> However, the investment ban was blocked by a US court ruling after Xiaomi filed a lawsuit in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Columbia" title="United States District Court for the District of Columbia">United States District Court for the District of Columbia</a>, with the court expressing skepticism regarding the government's national security concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Xiaomi denied the allegations of military ties and stated that its products and services were of civilian and commercial use.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In May 2021, Xiaomi reached an agreement with the Defense Department to remove the designation of the company as military-linked.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit_by_KPN_alleging_patent_infringement">Lawsuit by KPN alleging patent infringement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Lawsuit by KPN alleging patent infringement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 19 January 2021, <a href="/wiki/KPN" title="KPN">KPN</a>, a Dutch landline and mobile telecommunications company, sued Xiaomi and others for <a href="/wiki/Patent_infringement" title="Patent infringement">patent infringement</a>. KPN filed similar lawsuits against Samsung in 2014 and 2015 in a court in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit_by_Wyze_alleging_invalid_patent">Lawsuit by Wyze alleging invalid patent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Lawsuit by Wyze alleging invalid patent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2021, Xiaomi submitted a report to Amazon alleging that <a href="/wiki/Wyze_Labs" title="Wyze Labs">Wyze Labs</a> had infringed upon its 2019 "Autonomous Cleaning Device and Wind Path Structure of Same" robot vacuum patent. On 15 July 2021, Wyze filed a lawsuit against Xiaomi in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Western_District_of_Washington" title="United States District Court for the Western District of Washington">US District Court for the Western District of Washington</a>, arguing that <a href="/wiki/Prior_art" title="Prior art">prior art</a> exists and asking the court for a declaratory judgment that Xiaomi's 2019 robot vacuum patent is invalid.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asset_seizure_in_India">Asset seizure in India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Asset seizure in India"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2022, India's <a href="/wiki/Enforcement_Directorate" title="Enforcement Directorate">Enforcement Directorate</a> seized assets from Xiaomi as part of an investigation into violations of foreign exchange laws.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The asset seizure was subsequently put on hold by a court order, but later upheld.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions">Sanctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sanctions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsoring_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine">Sponsoring the Russian invasion of Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sponsoring the Russian invasion of Ukraine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a> Xiaomi reported the suspension of operations in Russia, but in July 2022, Xiaomi and its sub-brand POCO together held 42% of the Russian smartphone market, ranking first in terms of sales.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> On 13 April 2023 Xiaomi Corporation and 13 Xiaomi officials (responsible key management), namely <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lin_Bin" title="Lin Bin">Lin Bin</a>, Lu Weibing, Liu De, Zhang Feng, Zeng Xuezhong, Yan Kesheng, Lam Sai Wai Alain, Zhu Dan, Wang Xiaoyan, Qu Heng, Ma Ji and Yu Man, were listed by Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/National_Agency_on_Corruption_Prevention" title="National Agency on Corruption Prevention">National Agency on Corruption Prevention</a> (NACP) on their list of "international sponsors of war"<sup id="cite_ref-W&amp;S_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W&amp;S-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> because the company continued its operations in Russia after Russia's invasion and remained a leader in smartphone sales there.<sup id="cite_ref-W&amp;S_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W&amp;S-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Finland.27s_reaction_to_Xiaomi.27s_Russia_operations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland's_reaction_to_Xiaomi's_Russia_operations">Finland's reaction to Xiaomi's Russia operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Finland&#039;s reaction to Xiaomi&#039;s Russia operations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chinese smartphone brands continued to gain market share in Russia filling the gap left by Western brands which withdrew following Russia's invasion of Ukraine, according to a local retailer.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 September 2023, Telia, DNA, and Elisa, Finland's major mobile carriers, halted the sale of Xiaomi Technology products due to the company's ongoing business activities in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> This decision reflects the company's commitment to maintaining its operations in Russia despite the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Ukraine invasion</a>. The Finnish carriers' move came after Xiaomi faced several challenges in its European business in 2023. In March and April, Poland and Lithuania prohibited the sale of its products, while the European Union imposed sanctions<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> on Xiaomi's CEO, <a href="/wiki/Lei_Jun" title="Lei Jun">Lei Jun</a>.
</p><p>The sanctions imposed on Xiaomi are a component of the EU's broader strategy aimed at urging Russia to withdraw from Ukraine. In addition to this, the EU has implemented a ban on exporting various goods to Russia, including semiconductors crucial for smartphone manufacturing. Xiaomi's ongoing operations in Russia have sparked debate. While the company asserts its obligation to serve Russian customers and support its employees, some contend that it indirectly supports the Russian government financially.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_manufacturing">Overseas manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Overseas manufacturing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inaugural_plant_in_Pakistan">Inaugural plant in Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xiaomi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Inaugural plant in Pakistan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Xiaomi's mobile device manufacturing plant was inaugurated on 4 March 2022, to begin production in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. The plant was set up in conjunction with Select Technologies (Pvt) Limited, an Air Link fully owned subsidiary. The production plant is located in <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of July 2022, the future of the plant is uncertain due to the <a href="/wiki/2021%E2%80%932023_global_supply_chain_crisis" title="2021–2023 global supply chain crisis">2021–2023 global supply chain crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
